### [How to Value Land: Korean style!](https://www.progress.org/articles/how-to-value-land-korean-style/)
- **counters** [`objections/land-cannot-be-assessed`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-cannot-be-assessed/) — anchor: **“land can’t be valued separately”**
  - sentence: …One of the most consistent objections to Land Value Tax is that “land can’t be valued separately from improvements,” a complaint I initially addressed in my article series, later published as a chapter in my book, Land is a Big Deal.…
  - why: The essay presents South Korea's annual, parcel-level land valuation system as a direct counter-example to the objection that land cannot be assessed separately from improvements.
- **supports** [`objections/land-cannot-be-assessed`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-cannot-be-assessed/) — anchor: **“standard land parcels”**
  - sentence: …Korea’s “one special technique” is a particular focus on standard land parcels.…
  - why: The essay details the specific technical methodology (standard land parcels and adjustment tables) used to overcome the assessment objection.
- **counters** [`objections/lvt-invites-assessment-corruption`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-invites-assessment-corruption/) — anchor: **“each standard parcel must be valued”**
  - sentence: …In fact, it’s more accurate to say that MOLIT organizes the national effort, and crucially, the rules state that in all but exceptional cases each standard parcel must be valued by at least two different appraisal firms.…
  - why: The essay describes institutional safeguards—such as requiring dual appraisals and multi-level oversight—that mitigate the risk of corrupt assessments.
- **counters** [`objections/lvt-is-just-a-property-tax`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-is-just-a-property-tax/) — anchor: **“land values specifically, not just total”**
  - sentence: …South Korea , a country which not only regularly values all its land (and land values specifically, not just total property values), but which does so annually , and not based on broad regional bands, but down to the individual parcel…
  - why: The essay distinguishes the Korean system from standard property taxation by emphasizing its exclusive focus on land values rather than total property values.

### [How Well Can One Know Another? Even Oneself?](https://www.progress.org/articles/how-well-can-we-know-one-another/)
- **supports** [`objections/public-choice-critique`](https://progress.org/wiki/public-choice-critique/) — anchor: **“government planning and control”**
  - sentence: …One reason why government planning and control so often fail is that much of the economy is hidden from view.…
  - why: The essay argues government fails because it cannot access the decentralized, tacit knowledge hidden in the economy, echoing the public-choice critique of central planning.
- **supports** [`narratives/tax-land-not-labor`](https://progress.org/wiki/tax-land-not-labor/) — anchor: **“keep our full wage”**
  - sentence: …If we can keep our full wage and share the rent, we would all be able to choose our own bliss.…
  - why: The essay explicitly advocates for keeping the full product of labor (wages) while sharing land rent, which is the core definition of the 'Tax Land, Not Labor' narrative.
- **supports** [`narratives/community-creates-land-value`](https://progress.org/wiki/community-creates-land-value/) — anchor: **“share the rent”**
  - sentence: …If we can keep our full wage and share the rent, we would all be able to choose our own bliss.…
  - why: The essay's proposal to 'share the rent' implies that rent is a common fund to be distributed, supporting the narrative that land value is created by the community and should be returned to it.
- **supports** [`objections/land-cannot-be-assessed`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-cannot-be-assessed/) — anchor: **“much of the economy is hidden”**
  - sentence: …One reason why government planning and control so often fail is that much of the economy is hidden from view.…
  - why: The essay's broader theme that economic reality is 'hidden from sight' and difficult to measure supports the objection that accurately assessing specific components like land value is inherently chall

### [How YIMBYism Can Pave The Way For Georgism](https://www.progress.org/articles/how-yimbyism-can-pave-the-way-for-georgism/)
- **supports** [`objections/homevoters-will-block-lvt`](https://progress.org/wiki/homevoters-will-block-lvt/) — anchor: **“home owning Americans”**
  - sentence: …Reappropriating land rents remains anathema to most home owning Americans.…
  - why: The essay validates the objection that homeowners are the primary political barrier to LVT, citing the 'tax revolt' and the entrenchment of property as wealth.
- **supports** [`objections/lvt-needs-zoning-reform-first`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-needs-zoning-reform-first/) — anchor: **“existing land use regimes”**
  - sentence: …As it stands, implementing an LVT is a political non-starter.…
  - why: The essay argues that LVT cannot function as a supply lever where zoning is restrictive, predicting a political backlash rather than development if LVT is enacted without zoning reform.
- **supports** [`benefits/split-rate-increases-construction`](https://progress.org/wiki/split-rate-increases-construction/) — anchor: **“shifting taxes from improvements to land”**
  - sentence: …In a world where homeowners want – and are allowed – to densify their properties, shifting taxes from improvements to land imparts immediate, tangible benefits as well.…
  - why: The essay illustrates the mechanism by which shifting tax burden to land encourages development, specifically noting the synergy with legalized ADUs and density.
- **supports** [`objections/lvt-hurts-asset-rich-cash-poor`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-hurts-asset-rich-cash-poor/) — anchor: **“fear of being taxed out”**
  - sentence: …There's also a fear of being taxed out of one's home.…
  - why: The essay identifies the 'asset-rich, cash-poor' fear—specifically the risk of being forced out of one's home—as a core source of political resistance to LVT.

  - why: The essay explicitly lists 'land-based public finance' as a core constitutional principle of its proposed reform, directly invoking the Single Tax narrative.

### [I'm Lovin' It!](https://www.progress.org/articles/im-lovin-it/)
- **illustrates** [`problems/public-investment-capitalizes-into-land`](https://progress.org/wiki/public-investment-capitalizes-into-land/) — anchor: **“the city has thrown in”**
  - sentence: …And, the city has thrown in a brand new subway station, to the tune of some $2.4 billion (while the Second Avenue subway line limps along toward its long-awaited completion date of "whenever").…
  - why: The essay details how public infrastructure (the subway station) directly increases the value of nearby private land, which McDonald's then captures.
- **illustrates** [`problems/rent-seeking-drags-growth`](https://progress.org/wiki/rent-seeking-drags-growth/) — anchor: **“world leader in real estate speculation”**
  - sentence: …It's well-known that McDonalds (the world leader in the fast-food business) is, more to the point, a world leader in real estate speculation.…
  - why: The essay highlights McDonald's prioritization of land speculation over productive enterprise (operating the restaurant at a loss) as a prime example of rent-seeking.
- **illustrates** [`narratives/the-great-land-robbery`](https://progress.org/wiki/the-great-land-robbery/) — anchor: **“sold this year for $35.6 million”**
  - sentence: …The parcel was sold this year for $35.6 million.…
  - why: The massive profit from selling the land ($35.6 million) versus the tax paid ($174,000) illustrates the capture of unearned increment created by the community.
- **illustrates** [`problems/speculative-vacancy-wastes-cities`](https://progress.org/wiki/speculative-vacancy-wastes-cities/) — anchor: **“does it make sense to have”**
  - sentence: …Now, you might ask, with Manhattan real estate worth what it's worth, does it make sense to have a drive-thru, with a big parking lot?…
  - why: The essay points out the inefficiency of holding a valuable Manhattan site as a low-value drive-thru with a parking lot, demonstrating land underuse for speculative gain.

### [Ignorance, Apathy, and Greed](https://www.progress.org/articles/ignorance-apathy-and-greed/)
- **supports** [`problems/rent-seeking-drags-growth`](https://progress.org/wiki/rent-seeking-drags-growth/) — anchor: **“policy failure that needlessly reduces”**
  - sentence: …However, the government regulates pollution instead, a policy failure that needlessly reduces employment and economic growth.…
  - why: The essay describes how regulatory capture by special interests leads to inefficient policy outcomes, illustrating the concept of rent-seeking.
- **supports** [`narratives/the-corruption-of-economics`](https://progress.org/wiki/the-corruption-of-economics/) — anchor: **“special interests pay to legislate it”**
  - sentence: …Because of the tax and land-tenure systems. Why do we have those systems? Because special interests pay to legislate it.…
  - why: The essay identifies the influence of special interests on legislation as a root cause of systemic problems, aligning with the narrative of corruption.
- **supports** [`objections/public-choice-critique`](https://progress.org/wiki/public-choice-critique/) — anchor: **“incentives of the greedy dominate”**
  - sentence: …With the benefits concentrated among a few interests, and the costs spread among the whole population, the incentives of the greedy dominate the incentives of the masses.…
  - why: The essay explains why concentrated interests win over diffuse majorities due to rational apathy, which is the core of the public-choice objection.
- **supports** [`narratives/unearned-increment-narrative`](https://progress.org/wiki/unearned-increment-narrative/) — anchor: **“morally undeserved portion of income”**
  - sentence: …The desire of the owners and managers of polluting industries to avoid the social cost of their pollution is greed, a morally undeserved portion of income.…
  - why: The essay defines greed as taking more than one morally deserves, which parallels the Georgist narrative that unearned income is unjust.

### [Implied Consent](https://www.progress.org/articles/implied-consent/)
- **counters** [`narratives/the-great-land-robbery`](https://progress.org/wiki/the-great-land-robbery/) — anchor: **“implied consent by all”**
  - sentence: …The idea is that a person may not agree with some policies, but benefits from others, so it all evens out, and therefore there is an implied consent by all regarding government policies.…
  - why: The essay disputes the legitimacy of implied consent to justify government authority, challenging the moral foundation of existing land titles derived from state power.
- **counters** [`objections/lvt-is-socialism`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-is-socialism/) — anchor: **“supported anarchism or voluntary governance”**
  - sentence: …Although Spooner thought that his arguments against a governmental implied consent supported anarchism or voluntary governance under explicit contracts, there is another possibility.…
  - why: The author explicitly distinguishes the proposed governance model (enforcing natural moral law) from anarchism or socialism, countering the objection that Georgist governance is a form of socialism.
- **supports** [`narratives/single-tax-narrative`](https://progress.org/wiki/single-tax-narrative/) — anchor: **“government whose sole function is to protect”**
  - sentence: …Therefore if there is a government whose sole function is to protect people from coercive harm, and that government does not itself commit coercive harm both in its laws and its public finances, then no consent is needed.…
  - why: The essay argues for a minimal state limited to protection from harm, aligning with the Georgist view that government's proper role is to secure rights rather than redistribute wealth.
- **supports** [`narratives/land-justice-and-indigenous-reconciliation`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-justice-and-indigenous-reconciliation/) — anchor: **“no person should be above any other”**
  - sentence: …However, in human reality, there is no perfect governance, and people disagree on the details of law, and so, as a practical matter, if we take human equality to its logical conclusion, no person should be above any other.…
  - why: The essay's emphasis on human equality and voluntary contracts supports the narrative that just land relations must be based on equal standing rather than hierarchical authority.

### [In Memoriam: 125 Years Since Henry George](https://www.progress.org/articles/in-memoriam-125-years-since-henry-george/)
- **supports** [`narratives/land-speculation-causes-cycles`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-speculation-causes-cycles/) — anchor: **“why do these depressions happen”**
  - sentence: …Thus it was that the question occurred to him, why do these depressions happen?…
  - why: The essay recounts Henry George's foundational observation of recurring industrial depressions, which led to his theory that land speculation drives the business cycle.
- **supports** [`narratives/the-rentier-economy`](https://progress.org/wiki/the-rentier-economy/) — anchor: **“shocking contrast between monstrous wealth”**
  - sentence: …Years afterward George said that here “I saw and recognized for the first time the shocking contrast between monstrous wealth and debasing want.”…
  - why: This passage illustrates the extreme inequality and 'monstrous wealth' characteristic of a rentier economy, which motivated George's search for the root cause of poverty amidst progress.
- **supports** [`narratives/single-tax-narrative`](https://progress.org/wiki/single-tax-narrative/) — anchor: **“what is the true fundamental cause”**
  - sentence: …The second question was, what is the true fundamental cause of the enormous inequality in the distribution of wealth?…
  - why: The essay frames George's life work as the quest to answer the two central questions—depressions and inequality—that the Single Tax narrative aims to solve.
- **counters** [`objections/overpopulation-causes-poverty`](https://progress.org/wiki/overpopulation-causes-poverty/) — anchor: **“The country was not poor and overpopulated”**
  - sentence: …The country was not poor and overpopulated — far from it.…
  - why: The essay explicitly rejects the Malthusian explanation for poverty, noting the country was rich and sparsely populated yet still suffered from destitution.

### [In Memory of Dr. Fred Foldvary](https://www.progress.org/articles/in-memory-of-dr-fred-foldvary/)
- **supports** [`narratives/land-speculation-causes-cycles`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-speculation-causes-cycles/) — anchor: **“18-year real-estate cycle”**
  - sentence: …Dr. Foldvary was the first economist — due to his in-depth knowledge of the 18-year real-estate cycle — to have correctly forecast the economic crash of 2008 a full 11 years before it happened, back in 1997.…
  - why: The essay cites Foldvary's successful prediction of the 2008 crash as evidence of the predictive power of the 18-year land cycle theory.
- **counters** [`objections/bubbles-cannot-be-identified-in-advance`](https://progress.org/wiki/bubbles-cannot-be-identified-in-advance/) — anchor: **“correctly forecast the economic crash”**
  - sentence: …Dr. Foldvary was the first economist — due to his in-depth knowledge of the 18-year real-estate cycle — to have correctly forecast the economic crash of 2008 a full 11 years before it happened, back in 1997.…
  - why: Foldvary's accurate 1997 forecast contradicts the objection that economic bubbles cannot be identified in advance.

  - why: The essay argues that banking profits and credit expansion are fundamentally tied to lending against land values.
- **supports** [`narratives/land-speculation-causes-cycles`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-speculation-causes-cycles/) — anchor: **“make crashes inevitable”**
  - sentence: …When bankers loosen their credit requirements, they make crashes inevitable.…
  - why: The essay attributes the inevitability of economic crashes to bankers loosening credit to fuel land speculation.
- **supports** [`narratives/the-rentier-economy`](https://progress.org/wiki/the-rentier-economy/) — anchor: **“surplus cash goes to bidding up”**
  - sentence: …A lot of the surplus cash goes to bidding up the price of land , which homeowners like when selling, dislike when buying, and realtors always like since their commissioners are fatter even though their daily expenses are too (but who does t…
  - why: The essay describes how inflationary monetary policy channels surplus wealth into driving up land prices, enriching rentiers.
- **illustrates** [`narratives/the-corruption-of-economics`](https://progress.org/wiki/the-corruption-of-economics/) — anchor: **“The Fed Has to Know”**
  - sentence: …The Fed Has to Know If you want to know the worth of Earth, you must consider the price of land, not the rent for land.…
  - why: The essay illustrates the narrative of institutional capture by arguing the Federal Reserve withholds critical land value data to protect banking interests.

### [Indigenous Rights](https://www.progress.org/articles/indigenous-rights/)
- **illustrates** [`narratives/land-justice-and-indigenous-reconciliation`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-justice-and-indigenous-reconciliation/) — anchor: **“rights of original inhabitants”**
  - sentence: …The Declaration recognizes the rights of original inhabitants to self-determination, including rights to historic land.…
  - why: The essay details the UN Declaration and the struggle for indigenous land rights, providing the historical context for the intersection of Geoism and Indigenous justice.
- **supports** [`narratives/the-great-land-robbery`](https://progress.org/wiki/the-great-land-robbery/) — anchor: **“state governments originate in conquest”**
  - sentence: …The historian Franz Oppenheimer showed that state governments originate in conquest.…
  - why: The essay cites Oppenheimer to argue that modern state titles are rooted in the conquest and dispossession of native peoples, supporting the narrative that land titles descend from theft.
- **counters** [`objections/nationalization-solves-the-land-problem`](https://progress.org/wiki/nationalization-solves-the-land-problem/) — anchor: **“ownership of land is not a unitary absolute”**
  - sentence: …We should realize that the ownership of land is not a unitary absolute.…
  - why: The essay argues against the binary of state vs private ownership by decomposing land rights into a bundle, countering the idea that state ownership alone solves the land problem.
- **supports** [`narratives/community-creates-land-value`](https://progress.org/wiki/community-creates-land-value/) — anchor: **“rentals generated by public works”**
  - sentence: …The strands of the bundle include the rights of possession, rights to the natural rents, rights to the rentals generated by population and commerce, and rights to the rentals generated by public works and civic services.…
  - why: The essay explicitly decomposes land value into components created by population, commerce, and public services, supporting the claim that community activity creates land value.

### [Individual Sovereignty](https://www.progress.org/articles/individual-sovereignty/)

  - sentence: …The premise of human equality implies that all persons have an equal share of the benefits of natural resources, and that can be accomplished by collecting the economic rent of land, its yield when put to optimal use, and distributing that …
  - why: The essay explicitly advocates for the collection and equal distribution of land rent as a necessary implication of human equality and individual sovereignty.

  - why: The essay argues that equal rights to natural resources require distributing the economic rent of land equally to all persons.
- **supports** [`narratives/community-creates-land-value`](https://progress.org/wiki/community-creates-land-value/) — anchor: **“generated by the local population”**
  - sentence: …The local site rentals, generated by the local population, commerce, and public goods, would be paid to the community’s providers of civic goods.…
  - why: The essay identifies local population, commerce, and public goods as the generators of site rentals, supporting the claim that community creates land value.
- **supports** [`problems/land-rent-could-fund-government`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-rent-could-fund-government/) — anchor: **“provide the funding needed”**
  - sentence: …The multi-level federations of voluntary communities and associations would implement the collection of land rent and local rentals, and this geo-anarchism would provide the funding needed to implement the voluntary governance.…
  - why: The essay proposes that the collection of land rent is the specific mechanism capable of funding the operations of voluntary governance.

  - sentence: …However, none of that higher land value belongs in a mortgage.…
  - why: The essay illustrates the narrative that location value is produced by the community rather than the owner.

  - why: The essay advocates for distributing recovered land value as a dividend to improve welfare and reduce reliance on government programs.

### [Intervention Denial](https://www.progress.org/articles/intervention-denial/)
- **supports** [`problems/public-investment-capitalizes-into-land`](https://progress.org/wiki/public-investment-capitalizes-into-land/) — anchor: **“generation of land rent”**
  - sentence: …The biggest subsidy of all is completely ignored by intervention denial: the generation of land rent and land value by government’s public works and civic services, most of which is paid from taxes on wages, enterprise, and goods.…

### [Is a Sales Tax Voluntary?](https://www.progress.org/articles/is-a-sales-tax-voluntary/)
- **supports** [`benefits/lvt-can-replace-capital-taxes-without-efficiency-loss`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-can-replace-capital-taxes-without-efficiency-loss/) — anchor: **“taxing rent indirectly”**
  - sentence: …By taxing rent indirectly, the sales tax imposes a deadweight loss, whereas if the rent had been taxed directly, there is no deadweight loss, since land does not shrink, hide, or flee when taxed.…
  - why: The essay argues that sales taxes create deadweight loss by taxing rent indirectly, supporting the claim that shifting taxes to land avoids this loss.

  - why: The essay concludes that if consumption must be taxed, it should be on land rent, aligning with the Single Tax narrative of shifting the tax base to land.

- **supports** [`problems/speculative-vacancy-wastes-cities`](https://progress.org/wiki/speculative-vacancy-wastes-cities/) — anchor: **“highly valuable land, amply provisioned”**
  - sentence: …We look around in every city and see patches of highly valuable land, amply provisioned with services and infrastructure, sitting idle, or only being put to a fraction of its potential use.…
  - why: The essay explicitly observes that valuable urban land sits idle or underused, directly evidencing the claim about speculative vacancy.
- **counters** [`objections/overpopulation-causes-poverty`](https://progress.org/wiki/overpopulation-causes-poverty/) — anchor: **“Yet there is no shortage of land”**
  - sentence: …Yet there is no shortage of land, neither!…
  - why: The essay dismisses the idea that physical land scarcity causes unemployment, countering the Malthusian view that overpopulation or lack of resources is the problem.
- **supports** [`narratives/the-rentier-economy`](https://progress.org/wiki/the-rentier-economy/) — anchor: **“no place for him to work”**
  - sentence: …Why, then, can he not work for himself? Because there's no place for him to work or nothing for him to do.…
  - why: The essay illustrates the rentier economy by describing a scenario where access to land, not lack of labor or capital, prevents people from working.

### [Land-Value Commissions](https://www.progress.org/articles/land-value-commissions/)
- **illustrates** [`benefits/landlords-cannot-pass-lvt-to-tenants`](https://progress.org/wiki/landlords-cannot-pass-lvt-to-tenants/) — anchor: **“capitalized down as a lower purchase price”**

  - why: The essay demonstrates the economic principle that a recurring charge on land value is borne by the seller through price capitalization, not shifted to the buyer.

  - why: The essay argues that shifting fees to an annual land-value basis removes the disincentive to improve property, a core benefit of land value taxation.
- **supports** [`narratives/community-creates-land-value`](https://progress.org/wiki/community-creates-land-value/) — anchor: **“retain an interest in maintaining a good local environment”**
  - sentence: …The broker would share the increased value of the land, and so would retain an interest in maintaining a good local environment.…
  - why: The essay illustrates how aligning compensation with land value incentivizes stakeholders to support the community investments that generate that value.
- **supports** [`benefits/lvt-can-replace-capital-taxes-without-efficiency-loss`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-can-replace-capital-taxes-without-efficiency-loss/) — anchor: **“saving interest payments”**
  - sentence: …Land-value commission have the same benefit as land-value public finance in saving interest payments, as the borrower pays the land-value charge rather than mortgage interest.…
  - why: The essay highlights the efficiency gain of substituting a land-based charge for debt-financed lump sums, reducing total interest costs.

  - why: By acknowledging the existence and variability of assessor's land valuations—and using them to build a functional tool—the essay implicitly counters the objection that land value cannot be assessed.

### [Marginal-Cost Pricing](https://www.progress.org/articles/marginal-cost-pricing/)
- **supports** [`problems/public-investment-capitalizes-into-land`](https://progress.org/wiki/public-investment-capitalizes-into-land/) — anchor: **“increasing the land rent”**
  - sentence: …The ideal transit makes the city more attractive and productive, increasing the land rent.…
  - why: The essay argues that efficient public services like transit increase land values, which is the core mechanism of public investment capitalization.
- **supports** [`problems/public-goods-fundable-from-land-rent`](https://progress.org/wiki/public-goods-fundable-from-land-rent/) — anchor: **“provides the means to efficiently pay”**
  - sentence: …The higher rent provides the means to efficiently pay for the transit.…
  - why: The essay illustrates the Henry George Theorem concept that the land rent generated by public goods can fund their costs.
- **supports** [`benefits/congestion-pricing-reduces-traffic`](https://progress.org/wiki/congestion-pricing-reduces-traffic/) — anchor: **“ideal price is a fare just high enough”**
  - sentence: …In that case, the marginal cost and ideal price is a fare just high enough to eliminate the congestion.…
  - why: The essay explicitly argues for congestion pricing (charging the marginal cost of crowding) to manage scarce road or transit capacity.
- **supports** [`narratives/community-creates-land-value`](https://progress.org/wiki/community-creates-land-value/) — anchor: **“Landowners pay back to the city”**
  - sentence: …Landowners pay back to the city the higher rent they get from the public transit.…
  - why: The essay describes the ethical and economic loop where community investment creates value that should be returned to the community.

  - why: The essay describes Henry George's proposal to tax land and use the revenue for public benefit, illustrating the Single Tax narrative.

  - why: The essay uses the Landlord's Game to demonstrate how monopolistic land grabbing leads to failure, illustrating the dynamics of land speculation.

### [On Objective Public Finance](https://www.progress.org/articles/on-objective-public-finance/)
- **supports** [`problems/land-rent-could-fund-government`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-rent-could-fund-government/) — anchor: **“government does not initiate force”**
  - sentence: …Therefore government does not initiate force when it taps the land rent for public revenue, since the title holder only properly has the rights of possession.…
  - why: The essay argues that funding government through land rent is consistent with Objectivist non-aggression principles because land value is unearned.
- **supports** [`narratives/citizens-dividend-narrative`](https://progress.org/wiki/citizens-dividend-narrative/) — anchor: **“distributed equally to the people”**
  - sentence: …The rent should be distributed equally to the people in cash and in the public services of a limited government.…
  - why: The essay explicitly advocates for distributing collected land rent as a cash dividend to the populace.
- **supports** [`narratives/community-creates-land-value`](https://progress.org/wiki/community-creates-land-value/) — anchor: **“what man’s mind and labor does not produce”**
  - sentence: …Land rent is a surplus, and equality of rights implies an equal ownership of what man’s mind and labor does not produce: the benefit of land, which is its rent.…
  - why: The essay distinguishes land rent from produced wealth, implying it is a social surplus rather than a product of individual effort.
- **counters** [`objections/lvt-is-socialism`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-is-socialism/) — anchor: **“government does not initiate force”**

  - why: The essay counters the charge that land value taxation is socialist by framing it as compatible with free-market Objectivism and private possession rights.

### [Principles of an Optimal Tax Policy](https://www.progress.org/articles/principles-of-an-optimal-tax-policy/)

  - why: The essay explicitly states that LVT promotes economic growth and efficiency by encouraging the best use of land, directly evidencing this claim.

  - why: The essay explains that LVT capitalizes into lower purchase prices and replaces mortgage interest, supporting the economic mechanism that prevents the tax from being passed on to tenants.

  - why: The essay argues that public investment is only justified if it enhances productivity, a principle it applies to its advocacy for land value taxation.
- **illustrates** [`problems/public-investment-capitalizes-into-land`](https://progress.org/wiki/public-investment-capitalizes-into-land/) — anchor: **“The way to quickly revive”**
  - sentence: …The way to quickly revive the economy is to stimulate general demand, not specific demand.…
  - why: The essay critiques public works for distorting the economy, implicitly acknowledging that such works create specific land values rather than general prosperity.
- **counters** [`objections/lvt-needs-zoning-reform-first`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-needs-zoning-reform-first/) — anchor: **“increase the barriers that crush”**
  - sentence: …Government chiefs are inconsistent when they claim to want to stimulate the economy, yet they increase the barriers that crush investment and enterprise.…
  - why: The essay argues that removing tax barriers (like shifting to LVT) is sufficient to revive the economy, countering the view that zoning reform must precede tax shifts.

  - sentence: …Economists use the odd term “rent seeking” for the seeking of subsidies, privileges, and protection from competition.…
  - why: The essay defines rent-seeking as the pursuit of subsidies and privileges, aligning with the wiki's claim that this behavior diverts effort from wealth creation.
- **supports** [`narratives/the-corruption-of-economics`](https://progress.org/wiki/the-corruption-of-economics/) — anchor: **“financing comes from special interests”**
  - sentence: …While individuals do send contributions to parties and candidates, much of the financing comes from special interests such as corporations, labor unions, lawyers, and the financial and real estate industries.…
  - why: The essay argues that mass democracy is inherently corrupted by the need for campaign funds from special interests, illustrating the mechanism of political corruption.
- **supports** [`narratives/the-rentier-economy`](https://progress.org/wiki/the-rentier-economy/) — anchor: **“Subsidies to special interests”**
  - sentence: …Subsidies to special interests are economic rents.…
  - why: The essay identifies subsidies as economic rents, supporting the narrative that a significant portion of the economy is driven by rent extraction rather than production.

### [Rangel's Mangled Tax Tangle](https://www.progress.org/articles/rangels-mangled-tax-tangle/)
- **supports** [`benefits/lvt-can-replace-capital-taxes-without-efficiency-loss`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-can-replace-capital-taxes-without-efficiency-loss/) — anchor: **“shifting taxes from labor to land values”**
  - sentence: …These WFLs could decrease income inequality without any excess burden by shifting taxes from labor to land values, as much of today's inequality come from unequal land tenure.…
  - why: The essay argues that shifting taxes from labor to land values reduces inequality without the economic waste (excess burden) caused by income taxes.
- **counters** [`objections/lvt-is-socialism`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-is-socialism/) — anchor: **“don't like it when entrepreneurs to make a lot of money”**
  - sentence: …My guess is that welfare-state liberals (WFLs) don't like it when entrepreneurs to make a lot of money.…
  - why: The essay critiques welfare-state liberals for rejecting efficient taxes like LVT, implying their opposition is driven by animus toward successful entrepreneurs rather than genuine socialist goals.
- **supports** [`benefits/carbon-pricing-cuts-emissions`](https://progress.org/wiki/carbon-pricing-cuts-emissions/) — anchor: **“levy taxes on all pollution”**
  - sentence: …An alternative to an increase in marginal tax rates would be for the federal government to levy taxes on all pollution.…
  - why: The essay advocates for pollution taxes as a superior alternative to income tax increases because they correct social costs without deadweight loss.
- **supports** [`problems/rent-seeking-drags-growth`](https://progress.org/wiki/rent-seeking-drags-growth/) — anchor: **“waste caused by taxes”**
  - sentence: …The waste caused by taxes, which economists call the 'deadweight loss' or 'excess burden,' increases by much more than the increase in the tax as the total tax amount rises.…
  - why: The essay explains how high taxes on enterprise create deadweight loss that stifles investment and productivity, aligning with the claim that inefficient taxation drags economic growth.

  - why: The essay characterizes land ownership as a form of rent-seeking where value is extracted rather than created.

  - sentence: …Instead, we’ve had crony capitalism —the kind that allows some to live off the lives of others.…

  - why: The essay argues that the current economic system's treatment of land creates poverty amidst wealth, supporting the claim that rising land costs drive poverty.

  - why: The essay explicitly compares the global property boom to a contagion, illustrating the narrative that land speculation spreads and creates instability.

  - sentence: …Most of these real estate deals are swapping an existing asset. It’s a round robin, where the only thing that changes is access to finance.…
  - why: The essay argues that the real estate boom is driven primarily by credit expansion and debt rather than productive investment, supporting the claim that finance growth is land credit.

### [The 4 Major Land-Gain Income Taxes](https://www.progress.org/articles/the-4-major-land-gain-income-taxes-that-developed-from-georges-two-general-categories-in-the-1890-national-platform/)

  - why: The essay explicitly rejects the classification of land as capital, arguing that land gains are distinct from capital gains.

- **counters** [`objections/lvt-is-just-a-property-tax`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-is-just-a-property-tax/) — anchor: **“not a tax on land”**
  - sentence: …“The single tax we propose is not a tax on land, and therefore would not fall on the use of land and become a tax on labor.”…
  - why: The essay quotes Henry George's distinction between a tax on land and a tax on land value to refute the idea that the Single Tax is merely a standard property tax.

  - why: The essay describes the mechanism by which credit expansion distorts land values and triggers a boom-bust cycle, directly supporting the narrative that land speculation causes economic cycles.
- **supports** [`objections/cycles-are-credit-not-land`](https://progress.org/wiki/cycles-are-credit-not-land/) — anchor: **“monetary authority injects excessive new money”**
  - sentence: …But when the monetary authority injects excessive new money into the banking system, to the banks it is like additional savings, as they lower the interest rate to loan out the extra funds.…
  - why: The essay argues that the root cause of the cycle is the injection of new money (credit) by the monetary authority rather than land speculation itself, aligning with the credit-school objection.

  - sentence: …The conception of capital goods in the Austrian school has not been assimilated into neoclassical thought.…
  - why: The essay highlights a fundamental theoretical divergence between Austrian and neoclassical economics regarding capital structure, illustrating the narrative that mainstream economics has marginalized

### [The Corn is as High as the Subsidy's Aye](https://www.progress.org/articles/the-corn-is-as-high-as-the-subsidys-aye/)

  - sentence: …But land cannot hide, flee, or shrink when tapped for civic revenue.…
  - why: The essay explicitly argues that land is uniquely inescapable as a tax base compared to mobile factors like income and sales.
- **supports** [`problems/public-investment-capitalizes-into-land`](https://progress.org/wiki/public-investment-capitalizes-into-land/) — anchor: **“Civic works pump up land values”**
  - sentence: …Civic works pump up land values as the charges on property owners only pays for part of these services.…
  - why: The essay notes that public infrastructure increases land values, creating a subsidy for landowners who do not pay the full cost.
- **counters** [`objections/lvt-is-just-a-property-tax`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-is-just-a-property-tax/) — anchor: **“exempt buildings and other improvements”**
  - sentence: …It would have been much simpler and less costly to exempt buildings and other improvements from the property tax and simply levy a charge based on the current market value of land.…
  - why: The essay argues that taxing land alone is superior to the current complex mix of property-based levies, distinguishing land value taxation from standard property taxes.
- **supports** [`problems/land-rent-could-fund-government`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-rent-could-fund-government/) — anchor: **“tapping of land value for civic goods”**
  - sentence: …Californians could spare themselves these excess burdens by repealing Proposition 13 and replacing it with a constitutional law that replaces all taxes with truly voluntary user fees as well as levies on pollution and the tapping of land va…
  - why: The essay concludes that shifting the tax base entirely onto land value is a viable and superior alternative to current complex revenue systems.

### [The Gaffney Quantum Leap Effect](https://www.progress.org/articles/the-gaffney-quantum-leap-effect/)
- **supports** [`benefits/lvt-can-replace-capital-taxes-without-efficiency-loss`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-can-replace-capital-taxes-without-efficiency-loss/) — anchor: **“shift to land-value taxation”**
  - sentence: …The only way to eliminate the Gaffney quantum leap effect is to directly tax rent instead of indirectly taxing it via taxes on revenue and profits.…
  - why: The essay argues that shifting taxes from capital and sales to land value eliminates the 'quantum leap' efficiency losses caused by current tax systems.
- **supports** [`benefits/taxing-land-raises-productivity`](https://progress.org/wiki/taxing-land-raises-productivity/) — anchor: **“quantum leap up to dazzling productivity”**
  - sentence: …With the elimination of taxes on wages, sales, buildings, and entrepreneurial profits, the economy would take a quantum leap up to dazzling productivity.…
  - why: The essay claims that removing distortionary taxes in favor of land value taxation would result in a massive increase in economic productivity.
- **supports** [`problems/rent-seeking-drags-growth`](https://progress.org/wiki/rent-seeking-drags-growth/) — anchor: **“reduction in output”**
  - sentence: …There is a quantum leap down to much less production, because the land use has shifted to one which has less output.…
  - why: The essay illustrates how tax-induced distortions cause land to shift to less productive uses, thereby dragging down economic growth.
- **counters** [`objections/land-is-just-capital`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-is-just-capital/) — anchor: **“taxes on gross revenues”**
  - sentence: …Taxes on gross revenues are especially destructive, as they squeeze out the profit more than taxes on income, which is gains minus costs.…
  - why: The essay distinguishes the destructive effects of taxing revenue (capital) from the proposed solution of taxing land rent, implying land is not just capital.

### [The Game of Monopoly versus Equopoly](https://www.progress.org/articles/the-game-of-monopoly-versus-equopoly/)
- **illustrates** [`narratives/single-tax-narrative`](https://progress.org/wiki/single-tax-narrative/) — anchor: **“The Landlord’s Game”**
  - sentence: …The game was invented by Elizabeth Magie Phillips, a follower of Henry George, as The Landlord’s Game to illustrate how land monopolies create inequality and economic woes.…
  - why: The essay recounts the origin story of Monopoly (The Landlord's Game) to demonstrate the Georgist critique of land monopoly.
- **supports** [`narratives/citizens-dividend-narrative`](https://progress.org/wiki/citizens-dividend-narrative/) — anchor: **“distributed to the players equally”**
  - sentence: …If the game is changed so that the land rent is collected periodically, and distributed to the players equally, there would still be a game, but now there is no more gain from a land monopoly, and the players end up in a more equal financia…
  - why: The essay uses the game modification to argue that sharing land rent equally prevents inequality and bankruptcy, supporting the concept of a citizens' dividend.
- **illustrates** [`narratives/the-rentier-economy`](https://progress.org/wiki/the-rentier-economy/) — anchor: **“land monopolies create inequality”**
  - sentence: …The game was invented by Elizabeth Magie Phillips, a follower of Henry George, as The Landlord’s Game to illustrate how land monopolies create inequality and economic woes.…
  - why: The essay illustrates the mechanics of a rentier economy where landlords accumulate wealth at the expense of tenants through monopoly control of land.
- **supports** [`narratives/unearned-increment-narrative`](https://progress.org/wiki/unearned-increment-narrative/) — anchor: **“no more gain from a land monopoly”**
  - sentence: …If the game is changed so that the land rent is collected periodically, and distributed to the players equally, there would still be a game, but now there is no more gain from a land monopoly, and the players end up in a more equal financia…
  - why: The essay argues that the unearned gains from land ownership should be shared rather than privately captured, aligning with the moral case against the unearned increment.

  - why: The essay illustrates the political power of landed interests (Junkers) to capture government policy and subsidies, aligning with the narrative of economic corruption by landowners.
